Free Talk

Don't Want Freedom 232

— Qi Fan

Many people want freedom, talking about it all the time, and some are willing to exchange hot blood for it. But what is freedom? How can things living on this earth have freedom? Even our own feet can't leave the ground successfully. Moreover, this earth is such a small part of space. When we think of the vastness of the entire universe, we will only be ashamed of our insignificance, so what face do we have to clamor for freedom?

We won't have any kind of freedom. Death gives a fatal threat. When we think of death, all value is gone. What's left of freedom or no freedom? If we want to fly, we don't have wings. If we want to dive, we lack fish scales. Running makes us slower than horses or deer. Climbing trees makes us worse than monkeys. Wrestling makes us weaker than cows. Being ferocious makes us worse than tigers or wolves. Being greedy for money makes us worse than corrupt officials, local tyrants, and bad gentry. Hey, corrupt officials and local tyrants are also people. I said the wrong thing.

But what I mean is that our innate abilities are not great, and we can't do whatever we want. So it's best not to talk about freedom. Humans will never have freedom unless it's an unborn fetus in the mother's womb that has some freedom to speak of. As soon as they are born into this world, freedom will no longer exist. Because the establishment of freedom takes life as a prerequisite. Now, when solving the bread-and-butter issues of life is still a major problem, we can't talk about freedom.

Who in this world has ever had freedom? Who has ever had freedom? No one has. However, limited freedom, freedom permitted by law, that can exist, such as freedom of religion, freedom of speech, etc. But what does it matter if you have these freedoms? Moreover, many people's freedom results in many people's lack of freedom. Freedom that can have conflicts is not a good thing. For example, if people have freedom of speech, officials' behavior becomes unfree. If people have freedom of religion, missionaries are not free to force you to believe in their religion. That's not very appropriate.

So I want to shout out the slogan "Don't Want Freedom." We should all conform to the rules, without any personal freedom. Officials cannot freely arrest and kill people, cannot freely plunder money, cannot freely violate the law and harm the people. No one can freely sell out the country, buy Japanese goods. Everyone cannot freely donate to aviation to save the country, cannot freely buy aviation construction lottery tickets, and cannot freely dance and entertain to save the country. In this way, the situation in Chinese society might improve. I sometimes really think that China has been bad throughout history because it has been too free. Everyone has forgotten that they are a member of society and only knows themselves. The new society that will emerge will certainly not allow this kind of thought and feeling.

Untitled 233

— Ju Ren

Long ago, in a book discussing physics, I saw an explanation of the origin of menstruation. Our ancestors, living in caves, faced dark nights and strong winds. They hid, afraid to venture out. Only when the sky cleared and the moon was full would they emerge for some fresh air. Over time, this influenced women's menstruation, causing it to follow the lunar cycle, occurring once a month without fail. Only with "flowers before the moon" do we have stories of talented scholars and beautiful women; such is the law established by our ancestors. Therefore, the success of marriages is attributed to the Old Man Under the Moon!

An unwritten, widespread belief considers menstruation to be an ominous thing. When menstruation occurs, women are absolutely forbidden from stepping over scales, rulers, bushels, or other such everyday objects. A certain rickshaw puller, because his cushion was soiled by a female passenger, washed it and then burned paper ingots to dispel bad luck. Menstrual blood is apparently like a poison gas bomb, spreading misfortune wherever it goes. With mysterious taboos comes mysterious efficacy. The Portuguese imported "red-clothed cannons" were actually used in battle during the Chongzhen reign of the Ming Dynasty. The only magical item to defeat these cannons was women's menstrual cloths; when hung all over the city, cannonballs would not fly, and the cannon itself would crack. Tradition held this to be incredibly effective. Menstruation could also ward off lightning. A certain unfilial woman abused her parents-in-law, a sin so great that the Thunder God was sent down to strike her dead. The woman took a soiled cloth and covered her head, and the Thunder God dared not strike. These national essence experts of spiritual civilization, with a heart to save the world, could very well compile a book on the physics and chemistry of menstruation, achieving immortality alongside a certain president's Buddhist scriptures.

Menstruation can be seen but not spoken of. Even writing about it is almost impossible; such is the situation. Modern ladies in high heels and flowing qipaos can dance the foxtrot to the music. Yet, when menstruation is mentioned, they all blush. Their views are no different from the rickshaw puller who burns paper ingots to dispel bad luck. Since the May Fourth Movement, women's movements have shouted their slogans with earth-shattering volume, but to no effect. People don't understand why. I say: Just observe how menstruation still retains a mysterious significance, as if not going to the City God Temple to see about misdeeds or worshipping Buddha. It can be determined that the women's movement has no fate!

A few days ago, I received a monthly magazine run by a certain Mrs., with signatures like "Zhang Huang" Mrs. and "Li Zhu" Madam. The editor-in-chief also leads by example, going by the name XY Mrs. I imagine those Mrs. must also approve of the theory of menstruation as mysterious and the theory of the marvelous effects of menstruation.

Night of the Metropolis 234

— Sheng Huanming

On Saturday evening, the city, dyed charming by the lights, was excitedly bustling. On Avenue Joffre, blue gaslights and red neon lights hid by the sidewalks, smiling. A child afflicted with the urban paleness disease was shouting, mouth wide open, "Extra! Late Night News!" At the entrance of a longtang, an old man, so gaunt that only a layer of brownish-yellow skin remained, was holding a bowl of pitch-black "tap water," gulping it down...

A foreign sailor, humming "Lili Marlene," staggered out of a saloon, drunk. His leather boots scraped against the cement. "Rickshaw!" He raised his hand as if taking an oath, and three people leaned on each other like boneless skeletons.

Seven or eight rickshaws rushed over like a tide. A young rickshaw puller who had not yet "opened for business" was slapped for blocking the way. The rickshaw pullers who had gotten a fare had slight smiles painted on their faces, transporting their masters to North Sichuan Road to find "salty water girls" for the night.

A young woman with a well-balanced black, white, and red complexion had her arm linked in an old gentleman's arm. Glancing at the old man's small, eight-shaped mustache, she chirped in a charming little voice, "Xiao Zhou, you promised me the diamond ring; you must give it to me tomorrow!" They walked rhythmically together toward the French Park.

The metropolis, in the glaring light of the incandescent lamps, shone on a wandering foreigner—a White Russian (ten years ago, he never dreamed of being poor; now, even in his sleep, he dreams of the wealth of St. Petersburg). He muttered behind a couple, a man and a woman. Two coppers were scooped out from the young man's billfold, stuffed full of banknotes. In the darkness, a ragged, starving old woman, with a hopeful, bitter smile, followed close behind.

"Kind sir, kind lady, please spare a little!"

"What's the matter?" The young woman glanced at her "little treasure" beside her. "Linlin, I'm annoyed even by seeing Chinese beggars; look!"

"Me too. Chinese beggars are dirty and smelly. Get lost! I hardly ever saw a beggar in America."

At the entrance of a longtang on Mindeli, an old clerk walked in with his salary for the month. He was calculating whether he could remit a few yuan home after deducting food and lodging. Suddenly, a "skinning pig" darted out from the darkness, pointing half a rotten banana from his large sleeve at him.

"Hey, friend! You know what's good for you..."

The night of the metropolis was excitedly noisy.

Hometown Rain 235

— Tang Tao

The spring in Jiangnan is known for its frequent rains, often lasting seven or eight days at a stretch. People living in Shanghai usually do not feel the need for rain. Once it starts raining, the weather is so gloomy that no one can stand being cooped up in their small homes. But when you go outside, there are no mountains, no lakes, and no tender green leaves washed by the rain. Everything is better on a sunny day. Sometimes, a wealthy person's car speeds past you, and you have to return home covered in mud.

I remember when I first came to Shanghai to study six or seven years ago, the schoolwork was especially busy, often requiring self-study until the afternoon. That year happened to be particularly rainy, and the drizzling rain often disturbed my mood while reading. Although I wasn't like the elderly Qi Ming, who named his study "Bitter Rain" and sat inside sighing all day, I certainly had some thoughts of "hating and deeply resenting it."

However, such things only happen in Shanghai. When I was young and living in my hometown, when the spring rain fell like goose feathers, climbing to the top of the building for a view, the distant mountain scenery was shrouded in a misty rain... the fields in the rain were fresh and serene, making it hard to feel... but what was especially lovely was the nighttime. I don't know which year it was, but one spring, I and two farmhands rowed a small boat to a town ten miles away to see a community play. The performance ended at midnight, and we encountered rain on the way back. The boat moved slowly in the river pond, the lamplight was so dim that faces could not be distinguished, and the hull brushed against the vines and weeds on the riverbank, making a rustling sound. The rain hit the awning, sounding melodious, sometimes slow and sometimes fast, like listening to music, harmonizing with the farmhands' folksongs, "Pushing the awning on a windy and rainy night on the river bridge," truly making one feel transported.

These past few years, I have drifted to the city. Every time it rains, listening to that stagnant, dry sound, and recalling the rainy days of my hometown, I truly feel that even the sound of the rain has changed! The changes in human affairs, needless to say!

Carrot Top 236

— Jules Renard, translated by Lin Qu

Cat One (Continued)

The blast of the shotgun stunned Carrot Top. He thought the little hut had exploded. After the smoke cleared, he saw the cat at his feet, looking at him with one eye.

Half of the cat's head was blown away, and blood flowed into the milk cup.

"It doesn't look dead," said Carrot Top, "Damn beast, I didn't miss my aim."

He didn't dare move. The cat's one eye emitted a yellow glow, making him uneasy.

As for the cat, seeing that its body was moving, one knew it was still alive, but it didn't seem to want to struggle to move. It seemed to be intentionally dripping blood into the milk cup, and carefully not letting a drop spill outside the cup.

This was not the first time Carrot Top had slaughtered a living thing. He had killed some wild birds, livestock, and a dog for his own amusement or that of others. He knew how to do it. If the creature's life was strong, he had to hurry, get excited, become enraged, and, if necessary, fight it hand-to-hand. Otherwise, we would be invaded by that useless feeling of compassion. We would become timid. We would waste time in vain, ending up with no result at all.

At first, he only inflicted some minor abuse on it. Then he grabbed the cat's tail and beat it on the neck with the butt of the shotgun. He hit it so fiercely that each blow seemed like the last, as if it were the final blow of mercy to let it die sooner. The dying cat grabbed at the air with crazed paws, sometimes shrinking into a ball, sometimes silently relaxing and stretching out.

"Who ever told me that cats cry when they die?" said Carrot Top.

He became anxious. This was taking too long. He threw aside the shotgun, grabbed the cat with both hands, and desperately wanted to sink his fingernails into the cat's flesh. He clenched his teeth, his blood vessels bulging, and strangled it with all his might.

But he himself was getting breathless. He swayed, exhausted, and fell to the ground, sitting, his face touching the cat's face, his eyes staring blankly into the cat's one eye.

Two

Carrot Top was now asleep on his iron bed.

His family members and people who heard the news and hurried over to his house crowded into the small hut, inspecting the scene where this tragedy had occurred.

"Ah!" his mother said, "I used a hundred times my strength to tear that broken cat from his chest. I can assure you he has never held me so tightly."

As she described to everyone that barbaric impression—this impression that, later, when the family sat and chatted idly in the evening, would be like a fabricated story—Carrot Top was sound asleep, dreaming.

He dreamed that he was walking along a stream, the light of an inevitable bright moon sparkling and crisscrossing in the water, just like the long needles in the hands of a woman weaving something.

On top of the shrimping net, pieces of cat meat were scattered about, shining brightly through the clear water.

Layers of white mist glided across the pasture, perhaps hiding light spirits within.

Carrot Top put his hands behind his back, to prove to them that there was nothing to fear.

A cow approached, stopped, snorted, and then quickly ran away, the sound of its hooves shaking the sky, disappearing in a moment.

How quiet it would be if that talkative stream didn't chatter so much, didn't murmur and mumble, making him uncomfortable like a group of old women gossiping together.

Carrot Top, as if wanting to hit the stream to make it stop talking, gently lifted the pole of the shrimping net, and then many large shrimp surged up from the reeds.

The shrimp kept increasing, upright, shining all over, leaping out of the water.

Carrot Top, overwhelmed by pain, didn't know where to go.

Then many shrimp surrounded him.

They surged toward his throat.

They made some small popping sounds.

They had opened their pincers wide.

Page 18

The Process of Balancing Exchange Rate Premiums and Remittance Premiums 240

Recently, the market situation has often been characterized by high overseas interest rates, while remittance premiums have been excessively high. If this continues, it will not benefit the market. Financial industry leaders, aware of this trend among their peers, have recognized that this imbalance between foreign exchange and remittances not only distorts the market but also raises concerns from external parties. In reality, these actions by industry players are intended to reduce the hassle of handling and valuing physical silver, sacrificing small profits. This does not affect the market. However, at the twentieth general assembly of the industry, a discussion was held on the imbalance between foreign exchange premiums and remittance premiums, and measures were proposed to rectify the situation. It was resolved that member firms should exchange and settle physical silver coins with each other, and that amounts of 5,000 yuan or more should be personally counted, sealed in boxes, and verified for accuracy. Keys and other petty expenses would be provided by the remitting party. In this way, those who speculate in cash and inflate remittance premiums would lose their leverage, and manipulation would be impossible. As a result, remittance premiums would fall, and foreign exchange premiums would be able to rise freely, pushing up overseas interest rates.

Interest Rates Rise, Remittance Premiums Fall 241

[Saturday: Banks settle transactions simply.]

Yesterday's overseas interest rates were about 5 points higher than the previous day, opening at 8 points, the same in both the morning and afternoon. Remittance premiums, having lost their leverage, fell sharply. Yesterday morning, the market opened at 1.3 yuan, and by the time the market closed, it had fallen by 4-5 points to just 8-9 yuan. Foreign exchange premiums and remittance premiums in the market suddenly averaged out, without any heavy or light disparities. This was due to the effectiveness of the financial industry leaders' rectification efforts. The total volume of interest rate transactions in the morning market was over 4.1 million for transfers and over 1 million for new transactions. Continued arrivals of 53 packages of Ningbo white broad beans were still accepted by the Tianjin Gang at the original price. Yesterday's 1,000 packages of Wenzhou beans were all sold to foreign companies. The price for large grains opened at 4 yuan, 6 jiao to 4 jiao and 9 fen, and small grains opened at 4 yuan, 5 jiao to 4 jiao and 2 fen, a decrease of 4 to 5 jiao compared to the selling price of the first batch.

丨 Middle Sand White Drops Two Jiao 丨

At the association's listing, 100 packages of ordinary grade 24 coarse sand white were listed at 20 yuan and 2 jiao and 8 fen, a decrease of 7 fen compared to the previous listing. Only 30 packages of No. 20 middle sand white were listed at 19 yuan and a half, a decrease of 2 jiao compared to the previous listing. Two to three hundred packages of Hainan red were offered, with the higher ones at 13 yuan and 7 jiao and 2 fen, and the next highest at 13 yuan and 5 jiao and a half.

Oil Market: The Rising Trend of White Tung Oil Gradually Subsides 256

The white tung oil sales market is at its peak season. After the holiday, various places want to prepare inventory, and domestic sales are active. Hanshang foreign firms also continue to actively handle transactions. The wholesale price has increased from 16 yuan and 8 jiao per dan to 18 yuan and 5 jiao. The strength of the rising trend was initially impressive. However, after this surge, buyers seem to have restrained themselves slightly. Yesterday, according to a telegram from Han, the purchase price of Zhizhi tung oil opened by merchants has increased to 19 yuan and 3 jiao, and the selling price among merchants is still between 18 yuan and 5 jiao and 6 jiao. Even if it increases further, it will be limited. It is said that Zhejiang tung oil has also been driven by the Hanfeng and its momentum is also strong. Hanghang still intends to sell each chu at 24 yuan. The high price has led to sluggish sales, so it is proposed to change it to 23 yuan and 8 jiao. Although it is unknown whether it is accurate, it is inevitable.

Cloth Market: Decline in Serge Sales 257

Serge is a popular product due to the brisk sales of plain colors, which have transactions in both winter and summer. Initially, serge was imported from British, German, and American goods. Since French merchants have been transporting and selling it, the aforementioned goods have been hit hard because French serge is cheaper. However, since the brisk sales of Chinese goods, the sales of foreign goods have also declined sharply. Retailers of plain serge mostly purchase the No. 918 and Liuhe brands from Zhanghua and other domestic products. Yesterday, the domestic Zhanghua No. 918 serge opened at 3 yuan and 2 jiao and a half per yard in foreign currency.

Hardware: Influx of No. 2 White Lead Sheet Leads to Sharp Drop 258

As the tea market has plummeted, the sales of white lead sheet have also been greatly affected. The arrival of goods in this port has been surging, and the rich inventory is enough to supply a year's needs. Moreover, the business of military factories and cigarette factories is also limited. Because of this, there is a general impression of being in decline. It is currently estimated at 35 yuan per dan, but the market is still negotiable for confirmed businesses and large transactions. Other colors, such as No. 5, No. 9, and No. 10, can all be estimated at 35 yuan in the current market, an increase of one or two yuan compared to previously.

Slum Life Special Issue (Part 1) Amateur Musings

"Impoverishing the Non-Poor" and "Leveling the Uneven" 259

— Pu

Before our dear readers look at the contents of this special issue, we should first explain the motivation and hope for publishing the Slum Life Special Issue.

We recently felt that in the political and social issues we have discussed in the past, we seemed to have overlooked the most difficult and important problem facing China today: the poverty of the poor. We have no way to obtain accurate statistical figures, but the number of so-called "poor people" in Shanghai and, by extension, throughout China is, at the very least, based only on what we can hear and see, and we cannot deny that their number has exceeded the majority of the entire Chinese people. We deeply feel that this phenomenon is the biggest "internal" national crisis in China today. This kind of national crisis is not as urgent on the surface as those "external," easily arousing the attention of the people of the country and the international community, but its latent danger is precisely the main cause of internal and external troubles, especially the loss of cities and territories in the past two years. Seeing the current trend, the scope of this number of poor people will only increase, and at the same time, the government and the majority of the non-poor people in the country, in addition to following customs and doing a little charitable or quasi-charitable passive relief, almost no one pays attention to the fundamental work of improvement. Regarding this point, we should pay special attention to the government, because the major policies to improve the suffering of the people are not something that a few private individuals can do, and the use of government power is necessary to achieve results. However, examining all the work of the government in the past, there is too little progress towards this goal. The government has all kinds of unavoidable difficulties in dealing with external national crises, which are easy to gain people's understanding, but the government's fundamental work to improve the suffering of the people can also be said to be the most important responsibility the government bears to the people, and we have not seen the government have any determination to save the plan and implementation, which is really incomprehensible to us. Some people may say; "The government is currently focusing on suppressing the Communists, and only after the Communists are suppressed can all relief problems be carried out." It is not something we dare to oppose, but we hope that the government should pay the same attention to the work of improving the lives of the poor, and implement it with the same determination. If not, then I am afraid that by the time the Communists are suppressed, the country will soon be over. Will it not fundamentally lose the government's original intention of suppressing the Communists today?

Mr. Sun Yat-sen once said a most concise and appropriate sentence. He said, "The only purpose we hold is to level the uneven and make the uneven level." We see now how many "level the uneven" work the government has done. Even those in the government cannot deny that this fact is evolving in the opposite direction. To explain it in the simplest terms, it is not "leveling the uneven," but "impoverishing the non-poor and making the non-poor poor." The greatest motivation and hope for us to publish this Slum Life Special Issue is that we deeply feel that the increasing expansion of the scope of the poor is the fundamental internal danger of our country and nation. We should loudly appeal to expose the suffering of the poor as much as possible, hoping to prompt the government and a group of non-poor people to pay attention, so that everyone knows how to urgently seek ways to save the tragic situation of the poor. We firmly believe that no matter what kind of political system the government is under, if it does not pay attention to the "poor people's" problem, this government will collapse and will not last long!

Life

Hundred Thousand Living Corpses 260

— Yi Qing

Slums on Robison Road

Walking past the Big Ben on Xiaoshadu Road, continuing west, the houses on both sides of the road gradually, gradually became gray, sloping, low, and narrow. Black tiles, brown walls, and decaying fixtures, everything presents fatigue and death. There are no neat street trees, no beautiful decorations, no tempting music, no shining red lanterns, and no lively and healthy girls, the light of diamonds, the fragrance of powder. Here, there are only dilapidated shops, weak colors, the groans of hunger and cold, the miserable cries of disease, dilapidated roads, thin and gray-black people, and the stench of sweat and flesh. Robison Road is just like that, forever and ever, gasping for breath, half-awake and not asleep.

The famous Yinghua Lane is located not far from Xiaoshadu Road. Its honeycomb-like body occupies both sides of the road. Countless, cell-by-cell houses are filled with many suffering people wriggling. Although their spirits are so tired and their faces are so pale, they are still constantly working, constantly struggling, constantly sweating, and constantly gasping for breath. Indescribable tattered and ruined things are piled all over the ground; human breath, smoke, and stench are exchanged, stirring up the entire space, occupying it, suffocating everyone's breathing, it is just like a large pile of rotten melons, with countless flies and mosquitoes buzzing on it, and it is like a small pool full of sewage, with many larvae floating in the pool. However, it is the gathering area for the masses here, it is the essence of Robison Road!

Crossing Yinghua Lane, irregularly interspersed between the sparse houses are undulating wastelands. On the wasteland, in addition to the original graves and rubble and decaying grass, some people have borrowed a corner of it as a place to live, and some people have borrowed a small piece of it as a resting place for the bones of those who died without a home. So these useless gaps are the heavenly kingdom where the living and the dead who stay here can settle down.

On the smooth road paved with asphalt, cars, trams, carts, and wheelbarrows pass by from time to time. Dust and shouts pass by in bursts, but they can never bring back a trace of lively enthusiasm. The street lights accompany the streets, lying coldly in the silvery-gray light. Without the wailing of the whistle, there is no turbulence of the crowd. Here

Caojiadu at the end of Robison Road is a poor market, composed of all kinds of poor things. Hawkers' stalls are displayed on both sides of the road, one after another. Little People's Assembly

How to Relieve the Plight of the Poor Caused by the Decline in the Value of Copper Coins 262

— Proposed by Councilor Wan Qiuqun

(Copper Coins and Slums) Obviously, mansions and copper coins don't have much to do with each other. This is because the people living in mansions need commodities that humble copper coins cannot fulfill. In other words, the things they need are expensive and require silver to purchase. Therefore, they deal with silver and have little to do with copper coins. Conversely, our friends living in slums are closely related to copper coins. They mostly deal with copper coins, so the decline in the value of copper coins affects their lives and makes it harder for them to survive.

Currency is essentially a commodity. It contains a certain amount of labor. Its price decrease invariably leads to price increases of goods. Its price increase invariably leads to price decreases of goods.

Not many months ago, the price of copper coins was about 2,500 cash per yuan. Recently, one yuan can be exchanged for about 3,200 cash. This means that one copper coin now is only worth about 78% of what it was worth at its highest point. In other words, one hundred cash now is worth a little less than eighty cash at its highest point, essentially a 20% discount across the board. Therefore, the prices of many things have increased when calculated in copper coins, and friends in the slums who use copper coins are the first to suffer.

In the slums, no one suffers from the woes of copper coins more than ordinary rickshaw pullers, laborers, and peddlers. They cannot raise their fares by two copper coins because of the decline in the value of copper coins. A day's odd job still pays three or four dimes. Ham dumplings still cost twelve copper coins, and fried rice cakes are still three copper coins. Thus, the compensation for their labor and their income are effectively discounted by 20%.

With income reduced by 20% and suffering a 20% loss on spending due to the decline in the value of copper coins, life becomes even more difficult under this double discount. This is "unimaginable" to the young masters and misses in the mansions!

So, how to provide relief? That is a matter for discussion among the readers of this publication!

Such a Family! 263

— Shen Zhi

(Hut) Not far from a factory, there is a low-lying and damp open space, which can also be described as an open public pit. On this dirty open space, a small hut was built. This hut is truly pitifully small, with a length and width of only six or seven feet. The roof and the surrounding walls are all patched together with rags, bamboo, wood, straw, and rusty pieces of tinplate. Most of the materials come from "garbage bins." Because of the complexity of the materials, the technical difficulties are imaginable. Especially to avoid wind and rain, thick straw ropes must be used to intricately tie the entire house, like an added decoration.

The hut has a door facing the road, shaped like an upright egg, which is too short. Except for children, one must stoop to enter. Fortunately, the adults living inside have already become hunched!

Although there are no windows, there are many cracks in the surrounding walls, which not only allow some sunlight to penetrate but also allow rain to enter.

The people in the hut include a couple and two children, the older one being eight or nine years old and the younger one being two or three years old. The elderly couple is around forty or fifty years old.

The head of the family has an injured left eye, which is tightly wrapped with a piece of medicated cotton. His back is severely bent, and he coughs incessantly, even spitting out a mouthful of thick green phlegm. He often paces back and forth in front of his pitiful hut, as if he is filled with thoughts. His wife has a bundle of withered and disheveled hair – with absolutely nothing in common with the dishevelment of modern girls – covering her forehead and the back of her neck. Her face is even more terribly yellow and black, which is clearly a sign of enduring the hardships of life and malnutrition. She has no expression. No trace of sorrow or joy can be found. It is simply a rigid face. The two children are just two skinny monkeys, but definitely not as agile as monkeys.

Their clothes are exactly what is called "hundred-family clothes," just like the hut they live in, purely patched together with fabrics of all kinds. Especially the housewife's uneven-edged coat, which is only knee-length, just like the short cheongsams that were popular in Shanghai two years ago. She wears a pair of shoes with two different styles. Among the whole family, wearing shoes is her exclusive right.

Let's take a look inside their hut. It is simply a pigsty. On the ground in the western corner, there is a straw mat made of something like salt bags. In the pile of tattered cotton, there is a faint tremor, and at the same time, a broken and continuous wailing can be heard. It turns out that there is a living thing lying inside!

The south side of the hut serves as the kitchen. There is a stove made of a half-moon-shaped broken jar. In addition, there are scattered bowls and chopsticks. On the north side, some tools for making a living are hung, such as a plasterer's brush and a large manure basket for picking up garbage.

When it doesn't rain, they can cook outside. Do they have rice to eat? In a big pot, they boil the large leaves of amaranth – these large leaves are originally used to feed pigs, and in ordinary vegetable fields, we can see piles of them discarded like tombs – occasionally a few snow-white noodles float up from the turbulent boiling water, with only a trace of salt added. Oil is said to be off the agenda.

Their food is cooked, and they all sit on the ground to eat. Although there are only four people, there are bowls and chopsticks of all shapes and sizes! There is a cigarette holder, and a half-moon-shaped bowl. Taking advantage of their meal, I started chatting with the head of the family.

"Where are you from?" I asked him with sympathy and sincerity.

"Alas, sir!" He said with a mixture of sadness in his kind face, "I am originally from Shandong, but in order to escape the heavy burden of excessive taxes and levies, I had to leave my hometown almost eight years ago."

"What do you do?" I hesitated first, afraid of making him sad, but finally mustered the courage to say it. "What do I do?" He hastily swallowed a mouthful of food and replied, "Alas, sir! Now, you could say that I have a job, but I don't have a job; you could say that I don't have a job, but I do. I do a small job of painting walls. I rarely get a chance to do it a few times a month. The survival of my family of four depends entirely on me. My survival depends on luck!"

"How long have you lived here?" I continued to ask him.

"Sir! Let me tell you in detail," he had already forgotten to eat, his dim eyes shining with a soft light, staring at me, and said, "In the autumn of the year before last, I moved from Pudong to Zhabei, borrowing a hut that was much larger than this to live in. Although business was very bad at that time, I still hoped that it might get better in winter because in winter, many people have to brush their houses and prepare for the new year. Unexpectedly, later, the Japanese planes blew up our hut into powder. Fortunately, we managed to save our four lives and suffer here!" After saying these words, he stopped eating. He took out a bucket, turned it upside down, put a piece of clothing on it, and hurriedly asked me to sit down while still talking to me in depth.

"I used to work as a stevedore in Pudong, and I could only earn one or two dimes a month. We have lived like this for several years. But later, life became even more difficult. Until the year before last, there were more and more stevedores every day, and I was also a person without connections; at the same time, I was old, and I couldn't do the work on the wharf anymore! Therefore, I was kicked out! I have no way now, I can only wait for death! But I still hope that my two sons will grow up in the future, and maybe they can vent our grievances for us poor people!"

After he finished these words, he seemed even more depressed. His gaze had turned to the two children who were not wearing a stitch of clothing. I saw that he was too sad, so I took the opportunity to leave.

Mermaids 264

— Chen Lisheng and Zuo Yun cooperated

(Sampan) The lives of Shanghai people are truly diverse. The rich have the lives of the rich, and the poor have the lives of the poor. No matter what, they cannot be drawn onto the same line of life. Among the poor, there is an even poorer way of life, and that is the life in the sampans.

A sampan is a type of boat without a deckhouse. In the current situation of rural bankruptcy and an increasingly severe urban economic crisis, the sampan industry is bound to be in decline. Therefore, the life of a family in a sampan cannot be sustained by the stinky water in the river, and they must each find a way out. Men can only pull rickshaws, and women go to work in factories. But the life of pulling a rickshaw or working in a factory may not be satisfactory. Although there are many houses in Shanghai, they are enjoyed by the rich. Although the sampans are small, they are still useful for sheltering from the wind and rain.

Therefore, in every river in western Shanghai, there are many people who use sampans as their homes. Their houses rise and fall with the tides of the river. If the bottom of the boat has been around for a long time and cannot withstand the water seeping in, it can also be dragged to the bank and placed aground. Living in it is still not a problem, but it cannot be moved.

The inside of the boat, needless to say, is extremely cramped. During the day, a broken reed mat is removed from the side of the boat, allowing us to see the interior. Looking closely, we can see a pair of well-arranged chopsticks, a chipped oil pot, a broken soy sauce bottle, and a spatula with a broken handle. In short, the cooking utensils are all available, but they are just a little tattered. The belly of the boat is full of mud-stained straw and carrots. On the bow of the boat, two piglets are circled with bamboo strips, along with chamber pots, rags, tin foil, cigarette shells, cans of Le Tu Jing, high-heeled shoes with broken heels, and diapers, etc., all piled up haphazardly.

Some people also dislike the boat being too narrow, so they remove the original mat awning and piece together some lead sheets and wooden boards to build it like a house. This is a more aristocratic type of sampan, and it is also the result of their willingness to work. Because there are plenty of old goods at the junkyards, as long as you pay a little price. The source of this price is labor. Otherwise, if you are willing to rummage through more garbage cans, you can get them the same way.

However, there is one thing to worry about. When the early tide comes, you can't oversleep. Otherwise, other boat dwellers will wake you up and scold you because your boat is not being taken care of. If it leaves the dock, it will crush other people's awnings. If a sudden rainstorm comes, you must quickly set up the mat awning. Otherwise, if the rain gets into the cabin, you will have to sleep on the damp boards at night. When the wind rises, it is time to rock the boat. The whole family does not dare to leave, fearing that the cable will loosen and the boat will drift away. Therefore, living in a sampan is definitely not as quiet as living in a grass shed. It is also the poorest people who live in sampans.

Attention Unemployed Friends 265

A certain couple, the man engaged in translation work, and the woman teaching at a certain girls' school, use their spare time to voluntarily teach a poor, unemployed female student in exchange for taking care of a one-year-old child during the day, and can provide food and lodging and a small amount of pocket money. Anyone who is of good character and aspires to study, please send a detailed resume to Miss Liu, c/o Republican Girls' School, Menggu Road.

Central Enamelware Camp, Nos. 6, 7, and 8 South Old Garbage Bridge, now needs a street vendor who is qualified to promote enamelware signs. The salary and commission are generous. Those who are new to the job, please come to the camp and meet with Mr. Yao Gongyuan in person.

Tension 266

— Lv

(Workshop) Usually, when it gets hot, after work, most of the people in the workshop come to the alley to cool off. The older ones sit next to people and talk about how difficult it is to live in the world nowadays. Sometimes, when they get excited, they will also talk about the survival of China and the history of participating in the May 30th General Strike. The young male workers, besides talking to their partners about how hateful the rice buckets in the factory are and how the lackeys rely on their power to bully others, always talk about women. Some go to the young girls, waiting for a chance to chat with them. The child laborers are good at playing cards and rolling copper coins. The four- or five-year-old children, despite not knowing what is good or bad, play all day long. Their mothers are busy all day long sewing clothes, cooking, and washing clothes. In addition, there are a few people who run around everywhere after work and will not come back until night.

The stench from the garbage pile in the corner of the alley and the dampness from the houses, plus the sweat from the people, make the entire workshop a turbid mess.

But today, something seems unusual in the workshop. There is not the usual noise, and there are not as many people in the alley as usual. But there are many sighs coming from various rooms. Only the children are still playing as usual. The guys who usually run around everywhere after work are not running around today. Everyone is sitting at Geng Sheng's – one of them – house.

"Lao Sun told me about that," Lao Li, a tall man with dark skin, looked at the partners around him and said, "He said that three days ago, weren't three cars full of cotton yarn driven in from outside when we were eating? The cars stopped at the warehouse gate, and then someone carried the bales of yarn inside. Zhang XX from the factory was standing next to the car, and a guy who looked like a Japanese, acting suspiciously, not knowing what they were talking about. Someone went to ask what was going on, and they replied that it was transported from the old factory. But Lao Sun didn't quite believe it. He stole a gap and went outside for a walk, and then quietly told everyone that the yarn was transported from a Japanese yarn factory in XX Du. At that time, everyone was a little confused. Today, the capitalist announced that the cotton yarn business was not good and that wages would be reduced. I realized what was going on."

Everyone was a little indignant when they heard this.

"Just now, Xiao Liu from the fine yarn workshop told me when he was off work, let's tell the people in the workshop and the people living here about this matter. We want everyone to stand up and oppose the wage reduction," Lao Li took a sip of tea and said again.

That night, the entire workshop was different from the silent atmosphere when they came back from work today, and also different from the usual atmosphere. It was in an unusually tense atmosphere.

A Group of Strange Birds 267

— Ms. Lv

(Pigeon Coop Houses) In a pigeon coop house, there are two small-footed women working the night shift in the tobacco factory in the front building. On top of the front building is a young man who coughs every night, making it impossible for people to sleep. He is only twenty-five or six years old, but he is as thin as a skeleton. The landlord lives in the living room, and above the living room is a low cage called the attic, where I live. The alcove room is occupied by a couple who have just come from the countryside, who are said to be looking for work, but they have been living there for several months. As for who lives in the kitchen, I have not seen them for several months, nor do I have the time to inquire. This is life in the cage:

The landlord doesn't know what he does, and he is rarely seen. The woman plays mahjong at home all day, usually until after one o'clock in the night before she stops, which is especially distressing for me, who has to go to the factory during the day. Sometimes, I am very angry and want to scold her, but I finally endure it. Compared to her, she is still not as hateful as our foreman. Our foreman is really a fierce god! Being late is punished with beatings and scolding and fines, and being slow is also punished with beatings and scolding and fines. Sometimes I have such thoughts in my heart: "Bring a knife and chop down from the top of that foreman's head," as if that would relieve my anger. But I know that even if I kill her alone, it won't work, because there are more foremen oppressing us. If one dies, there will be a second one to come. Therefore, unless we, the oppressed people, unite to resist them, individual resistance will have no result.

The couple in the alcove room is really inexplicable. Sometimes I hear them laughing loudly, sometimes I hear the man scolding, and sometimes I hear the woman shouting for death. Cups and bowls sometimes fly out of the window, and glass is sometimes shattered. The landlady scolds and wails, but immediately disappears without a trace. The quarreling stops, and the crying stops. It's really strange, why is life between the two sexes so incompatible!

Speaking of myself, I have to get up before dawn to go to the factory in the morning. I hurriedly cook a little rice, and the vegetables were bought the night before, perhaps dried radish or pickles. I carry my lunch basket and run, not waiting for the factory to ring the bell, and must rush to get there. Once I go in, I am released only after twelve hours. When I get home, I am almost like a half-dead person, and I eat something casually and fall on the bed to sleep. I am doing this as a slave to the machine, and I don't know when I can get a rest! The two small-footed women in the front building are rarely seen two or three times a month. When they come back, I go out, and when I come back, they go out. Only on the road can we occasionally meet. One is said to be the sister-in-law, whose brother was washed away when there was a big flood; the other is the younger sister, about seventeen or eighteen years old, but she is black and thin. The wages they earn, in addition to sending some to the grandmother at home, also have to send three yuan a month to the introducer. They themselves have nothing left.

The young man in the attic above has recently lost his job. He used to work in the XX Iron Factory. I'm not very clear about the rest, but I occasionally wake up in the middle of the night and hear the landlady talking about him in the "pong, east wind" mahjong game. It seems that he has already owed two months' rent.

Humble Lives 268

— Ms. Yi Shan

(Under the Eaves and Under the Staircase in the Alley) I live in a wharf area. Because it is close to the wharf and has many bathhouses, pancake shops, and a small vegetable market, it has become a gathering place for wharf laborers. If you pass through this place, you will see workers of all shapes and sizes everywhere with rotten eyes, crooked noses, and swollen red faces. In the morning, evening, and on holidays, the streets and alleys are filled with them. Not to mention cars and rickshaws, even people walking by have to push left and dodge right, making many detours to pass through.

These laborers all have no homes. During the day, they sell all their labor at the wharf. When they come back in the evening, they randomly fill their stomachs and then lie down under the eaves on both sides of the road and under the staircases in the alley to sleep. In rainy weather, they endure the light rain, and in heavy rain, they sit and sleep in the crowded staircases in the alley or other places that can provide some shelter. The price of their hard work all day cannot afford them to stay in a small inn. In fact, they are lucky if they can avoid starvation. All year round, from spring to summer, from autumn to winter, in the cycle of the four seasons, they stiffly drag their humble lives. At most, they spend three or four copper coins to buy a bowl of alcohol-laced water to stimulate their numb nerves. Some who cannot afford opium spend ten copper coins to buy opium residue water, which is boiled with the residue of opium dregs that have been cooked into opium paste. It is even more blood-sucking and bone-gnawing than opium. Those laborers who eat pancakes and steamed buns and have no fat in their stomachs become addicts in just four or five days and soon become active mummies.

Although they work hard all year round, they eat pancakes, steamed buns, or rotten fish and meat, and sleep in the streets and alleys. No matter how strong their bodies are, their lives cannot last long, especially since they are also having their vitality sapped by alcohol and opium residue water. Therefore, I often see laborers lying down and groaning painfully by the dirty small roads or in the damp and smelly alleys. Then, the next day or four or five days later, they lie straight and won't move until the police discover them and send someone to carry them to some unknown place. And those animals of the same kind who are still alive, they are still working, drinking alcohol, drinking opium residue water, living numbly and despairingly, waiting until one day they also lie down and won't wake up.

Special Announcement from this Publication 269

The theme of this publication remains "Life in the Slums". We hope that all sectors will actively submit manuscripts. Your anticipation is greatly appreciated! Compensation is generous.

Guest on the Seat 270

— Long Yi

Attic

I am twenty-four years old. At the age of sixteen, I left my remote and distant hometown to advance towards this vast world and open the door to life. For seven or eight years, I have traveled all over the north and south of the Yangtze River, the three Xiang and seven Ze, and the Han, Luo, You, and Yan regions. I am pursuing, pursuing, and pursuing the future I yearn for.

Life seems to expand forward like the ripples caused by a stone thrown into the calm water, but gradually it contracts inward. This band of life binds me tightly, like being sealed in a can. But I still want to struggle and break through this solid wall.

In this big city, the rich are fascinated by their greedy eyes, the young masters and misses are dancing their delicate and amorous eyebrows, the merchants are holding their iron-faced and ruthless abacuses, and my young friends, like me, are vying for opportunities in the streets, like playing hide-and-seek to find a piece of bread to fill their stomachs. I, too, am struggling on this line of hunger like them. Today, I can still take refuge in the attic of a poor friend. Tomorrow, we will be thrown into the streets, deprived of any support.

Although I have no specialized skills, I have gained some experience in life and developed some abilities to cope with the world in the seven or eight years that I have been finding my own bread. In the past, I have worked as a secretary, copyist, proofreader, editor, teacher, and civil servant. Now, in addition to being able to do the above work, I also want to do other work. I am even willing to be an industrial worker, because I don't want my life to remain permanently in the atmosphere of intellectuals. My requirements for life are very low. Forgive me for not pricing myself in advance. If employed, I will be deeply grateful. Please forward replies through this publication. I am waiting with an empty stomach.

People Without a Country to Love 271

— Xiao Tang

(???) It was a deep evening, just before the end of spring, around one o'clock. The cold, crisp, and desolate wind wandered alone through the once-bustling avenue. I followed this wandering wind and walked onto the north end of the Sichuan Road Bridge. Under the south end of the bridge, wriggling black shadows were visible, trembling in the clear, cold electric light. At a glance, I knew they were three so-called "little three" types, taking advantage of the night to ply their "taxi-hailing" trade. A sense of curiosity – really, it was boredom – gradually drew me closer to them. I bravely began the first words of "conversation" with them, imitating the tone of a "tycoon."

"How much money can you earn each day pulling rickshaws like this?"

"It's hard to say. On a good day, we might make one or two thousand cash, but on a bad day, we barely make a hundred or two." One of them, about fifteen or sixteen years old, hesitated, glancing at me a few times before slowly answering. "Oh, we have to hand in five hundred cash every day!" A child of about ten years old, with not a trace of color in his face, innocently and frankly blurted out.

"What, you have to hand in money? To whom?" I asked in genuine surprise.

"Hmph! Of course, we have to hand in money, to 'Uncle'! We have to hand in five hundred cash every day!" the child replied again.

I was then sadly convinced that their handing in money was not a fabrication, because I knew at least something about Shanghai, and I knew that "Uncle" was one of the famous figures in Shanghai.

"So, after handing in the five hundred cash, do you have any money left? And what happens when you have a bad day?"

"'Uncle' doesn't care if we have a bad day. All 'Uncle' cares about is that we hand in the five hundred cash every day. We all have an 'Uncle.' I've sworn allegiance to my 'Uncle,' and those two have their 'Uncles' too. How can you 'hustle business' without swearing allegiance to 'Uncle'? Would you dare come here if 'Uncle' didn't agree? " The child said in a string, and excitedly continued, "We have to hand in five hundred cash every day. If you can't hand in five hundred cash today, 'Uncle' will beat you to death! Oh! Mommy! 'Uncle' beats so hard it's life-threatening!" As he spoke, the child pulled up the cuff of his right trouser leg and continued, "Look! Look! Mother X. The welts on my body hurt so much I cried for help, and they're still tingling. Alas, alas, 'Uncle' beats so hard it's life-threatening. He locks you up alone and beats you with whatever he can grab. Who's going to come and talk him out of it?" The child tried to pull his trouser leg up, but it was too small, too tight, and he was afraid of tearing it, so he just held it at the bend of his knee. He involuntarily rubbed his buttocks and the back of his thigh repeatedly.

The older one interjected, "We have to hand over all the money we get to 'Uncle.' If he finds any hidden money, it's another disaster. The clothes 'Uncle' occasionally gives us are just like the dirty old clothes we're wearing." He looked at me with pitiful eyes. The oldest one never answered me a single word, just sizing me up with triangular eyes.

"So, how did you end up in such a destitute situation? Do you pull rickshaws on the bridge every night? Do you sleep at 'Uncle's' house?"

The child was always innocent and straightforward, and he answered again, "We all ran away. Either our parents are too poor to feed us, or we were beaten too badly by the teachers in the apprenticeships. Running away here is really miserable. We have to pull rickshaws until dawn. When we sleep, any dirty, cold, and remote corner is our bed. We never know in advance where we'll be sleeping tonight. 'Uncle's' house is for the 'Uncles'; we've never had a home, and we don't know what a home is. It used to be a little better for us. Now, we can't 'hustle business' during the day because if the police see us, they'll arrest us. Being locked up in the police station for at least twelve hours, cold and hungry, is like losing half our lives, so we have to take advantage of the late night to do some business in hiding."

Laughter came from the top of the bridge. Five rickshaws came up in a row. The three children jumped up and ran towards them. Sitting in the rickshaws were three dancers and two young men. The young men were wearing red and green paper hats and singing the "Romance of the Spinning Palace" song. The dancers' laughter was sharp and shrill, like the wail of a ghost. A group of racing black shadows poured down the bridgehead. Two coins were thrown from the rickshaws, because I heard two clear clinking sounds as they hit the ground. The children chased after them, shouting and scolding. One of the young men raised his hand, as if throwing something at them. A tall police officer's figure appeared like a ghost, and the children disappeared in panic into the dark alley.

Supplement to the Shanghai Newspaper Local News Section

Film Special

Sunday, June 4, Year 22 of the Republic of China

Upside Down World During the Hollywood Earthquake 272

— Wen Ying

Tragedies, Comedies, and All Sorts of Things

Monsters and Gods in the Beauty Salon

At 5:55 PM on March 10th of this year, a strong earthquake occurred in Hollywood, USA. Although the shaking lasted for only a minute, the sudden shock caught the figures in the film industry off guard, and they unwittingly performed all kinds of strange dramas, including many tragedies and many jokes, in all sorts of ways, too numerous to mention. Now, I will only briefly describe some of the more important events.

Let's first talk about the injuries caused by the earthquake. Peggy Hopkins Joyce, known for her multiple marriages and romances, had a large burn on her face. At that time, she was curling her hair with curling tongs. When the unexpected earthquake struck, she lost her grip and pushed the red-hot tongs onto her face, resulting in a burned face. Jocelyne Lee was taking a shower at 5:55. Unexpectedly, her foot slipped, and she fell backward, like a kite flipping over, landing on her back. As a result, two vertebrae were dislocated, and she had to stay in the hospital for several days. There was also a very dangerous Anita Page. She was getting dressed upstairs, preparing to go out for dinner. After she finished dressing, she stood at the top of the stairs and talked to the people downstairs. The earthquake struck suddenly, and Anita fell down the stairs. She rolled from the top of the stairs to the bottom. She was bruised all over, and her legs were also swollen.

There was also Elissa Landi, who had been ill for a long time. Around six o'clock that day, she was still lying in bed when suddenly the mirror on the wall fell down, and the things in the room shook. Elissa and her mother ran outside together. Because she had been sick for a long time, she was suddenly shocked by this, and her illness became more severe. The above are some tragedies, but what about comedies?

Lillian Lashman said that the best place to see comedy during an earthquake is in a beauty salon. That day, she was getting dressed up in the beauty salon and was about to open the door to leave when the earthquake suddenly struck. Most of the women had white powder and blue mud smeared on their faces. Some had their hair disheveled, and some had their hair half-curled. They frantically pulled their hair off the curling irons. Everyone ran towards the door together. Lillian Lashman not only forgot her fear but burst out laughing.

Adrienne Ames was putting on lipstick, preparing to go out for dinner. She held the lipstick brush, carefully drawing on her lips, when suddenly there was a jolt, and the brush drew a line from her mouth all the way to her ear. She didn't realize it and rushed downstairs to escape. A maid saw that her mouth had a large crack that ran all the way to her ear and cried out in fright.

In addition, there were many other interesting things, but unfortunately, I can't write them all out.

Film Review

Review of "Roar of the Tiger, Roar of the Lion" 273

— Ling He

The Big Cage

Another animal movie.

If someone were to ask, "Why do European and American filmmakers always like to make animal movies? Is this educational film?" Then we can answer him like this: "This is escapism. At the same time, entrepreneurs are well aware of the needs of cowardly audiences to escape reality, so everyone dares not face reality squarely and contentedly watches wild animals fight."

Of course, if film artists can sincerely, based on educational significance, give a detailed and clear explanation of various beasts, then we are attending class when we watch movies. However, European and American colleagues will not do this. In their production process, this kind of animal film must be "horrifying," "tense," with animals fighting animals, people fighting animals, and also adding beautiful women's legs, sensual embraces, and passionate kisses. As a result, children laugh loudly, young men and women become more affectionate, and old people gain more knowledge. This is how it can be a box office success, this is how it can make money. However, watching too many of these films is inevitably dizzying.

As mentioned above, this has become a formula, which can be applied in "Tarzan the Ape Man," which can be applied in "Nagara," and this "Roar of the Tiger, Roar of the Lion" is naturally no exception, and of course, it is very applicable. Following the formula, change the title, and it's another set.

Regarding this film, according to the advertisements, there are indeed sixteen lions and sixteen tigers, but there is no way to count them clearly on the screen. However, these lions and tigers are the spirits of this film. Indeed, if we regard this film as a circus, then it is somewhat interesting. Lions biting tigers, tigers biting people, and people beating lions and tigers are very good to watch. In addition, there are gunshots, water sprays, lightning, thunder, storms, people running away, and desperate screams. It is truly "tense" and "horrifying" at the same time. Of course, this is because the director understands this formula.

However, in addition to the above points, the director simply did not use the method of montage for the development of the plot, and the connection between the characters before and after is not obvious. In fact, although there is a story, this story has no system at all.

As for the performance and other aspects, except for the protagonist's amazing skill in taming wild animals, there is nothing to commend.

In short, if you regard this film as a circus, you can be happy.

Powerlifter Peng Fei, the male lead in Yihua's new film "National Survival"

"Where to Go" Renamed "National Survival" 274

— Yin

Yihua Film Company's debut film, which has been promoted for a long time, is directed and written by Chen Yu. The leading actors are all famous figures on the stage (such as Shu Xiuwen, Hong Dou, Zhao Yishan, etc.), as well as powerlifters Zha Ruilong and Peng Fei. After more than half a year of work, it has now been completed. It will soon be released in Shanghai. However, the original name of the film was "Where to Go?" It is said that it has now been renamed "National Survival."

Audience Opinions

Written to the Screenwriters of "Spring Water, Affectionate Waves" 275

— Wu Cheng

Several new films from the Star Film Company this year, such as "Flower of Freedom," "Raging Torrent," "Women's Cry," "Moral Treasure Mirror," and "The Future," have made us feel that the Star Film Company is changing its style. The audience is very gratified and hopes that the Star Film Company can continue to work hard.

"Spring Water, Affectionate Waves" is said to be Zheng Zhengqiu's successful work after "Flower of Freedom," but in fact, it has left us completely disappointed. Although the direction, editing, photography, and set design are all commendable, and the actors are all working very hard, it is difficult to achieve full results under the control of such a plot. Because the meaning is really too unsound. How can a good play be developed from such a multi-faceted love story?

According to the usual practice, this should depict the hidden pain suffered by women under the moral system of the old society and indicate the path that new women should take. But in fact, the focus has shifted. The screenwriters are not focusing on what should be done, but are working hard on the behavior of the idle class playing with women. Moreover, narrow-minded humanitarianism, revengeism, and the law of karma are even more wrong.

Star's New Film "Iron Plate Record of Red Tears" 276

— Jia Nan

The mission of film is by no means just to provide entertainment for a portion of the idle class. It should provide for general needs and represent the appeals of the masses. The Chinese film industry seems to have this "awareness." In addition to the already released "Humanity," "Struggle," "Endeavor," "Women's Cry," and others, the Star Film Company will soon release a new film of the same meaning, "Iron Plate Record of Red Tears," which describes the tragic situation of the Sichuan people under the iron hooves of warlords who oppress and extort taxes, and represents some weak groans of the local Adou. This film is directed by Hong Shen, and the female lead, Ms. Wang Ying, has already had excellent achievements in drama and has also had good results in film. The male lead is Chen Ningqiu, who is famous in the drama world. The rest of the actors are more than twenty Fudan students who have been under Hong Shen's guidance for a long time. Undoubtedly, this film will give us a greater understanding. They are going to other places tomorrow to shoot exterior shots. In the near future, this film will appear before us.

Letter to Chen Du Jun: I have received your letter and read your manuscript, which has unique insights. Unfortunately, this publication is limited by its position and does not publish any text attacking any publication or individual. And all texts such as "dedicated to" or "advice" are also avoided. For example, saying "Please have a slap in the face" or "Here's a big slap in the mouth for you"; after hitting someone, you still want to make yourself look good, saying something like "please" or "here's," isn't that too hypocritical? My opinion is that if you really have the sincerity to contribute something, go visit them in person, have a long talk, and then slap them a few times and give them a slap in the mouth. I must first have the intention of a head-on blow, and people will then be able to accept it with an open mind. I don't know what you think.

Published as Received 277

To the Editor: In the "Recent News from the Film Industry" written by Zhou Jingzhi and published in your publication on the second of this month, it says that "Yihua Company, independently founded by Tian Han, will soon complete its first production, 'Where to Go,' etc." Our company is also named Yihua Film Company, and the founders are the well-known powerlifters Zha Ruilong and Peng Fei. There has never been a Tian Han, and the first production is "National Survival," which has now been completely completed and will soon be released, and it is not directed or written by Tian Han. To avoid misunderstandings from the outside world, we hereby send this letter and ask that it be published in your publication. Thank you very much. Respectfully, Yihua Film Co., Ltd.

Editor's Note: The above news is a contribution from the outside world, which sometimes leads to inaccuracies. The editor has the duty to record what he has heard and cannot reject them all or verify them in advance. For contributors, there is little to be gained, but for the parties involved, reputation and credibility are greatly affected, and the editor suffers even more trouble. As for this news, we should ask the original author, Mr. Zhou Jingzhi, to confirm whether there is another Yihua Company founded by Tian Han. Otherwise, rumors and gossip will be sent to this publication in a jumble. Although this publication has already disclosed it, the manuscript fee will also be deducted. I'm not good at this.

Overview of Soviet Russian Films (7) 278

— Written by Rudolf Meser, translated by Bao Han

"Regarding the production policy of Soviet film factories, they are now striving to produce 'sound films' to prepare for competition in foreign markets. These 'sound films' are different from 'talkies.' Today, Soviet Russia is concentrating its efforts and striving to manufacture them as a standard for selling overseas. 'Road to Life' was the first experiment in manufacturing sound films for foreign sales, and it has achieved great success. Here, I want to say something... but as I said before, I don't want to involve personal opinions, so there are always meanings that are not fully expressed. While the Soviet Union is striving to produce sound films, it must also strive to produce silent films, because silent films are convenient for travel and can be shown in remote villages and towns as a supreme tool for propaganda. (As for sound film equipment, today, only advertising claims that it is suitable for travel.

㈤ The attitude of Soviet Russia towards imported goods

British, American, and most German films are not very popular in Soviet Russia. The reason is that most imported films are not in sync with the spirit of the Soviet five-year plan; this reason is also to be fundamentally correct under the current situation in Soviet Russia. The German film "Comradeship" (Kameradschaft) and another silent film called "Rasputin" (also a German production) were widely broadcast in Soviet Russia. The film "Comradeship" has the meaning of cosmopolitanism, which is quite suitable for socialist countries to enjoy, and a film that can give a true depiction of the historical events of Rasputin is of course also easily welcomed. These films are all anti-despotic propaganda, and it is no wonder that they can be a sensation in Soviet Russia. But there are also things that are incomprehensible. "Dr. Jekyll," starring Harold Lloyd (i.e., Luke), was actually welcomed everywhere in Soviet Russia. "Dr. Jekyll" was an early work by Harold Lloyd, with extremely rich jokes. It came to Russia in the summer of 1932, and everyone rushed to show it. What is incomprehensible is what relationship does Harold Lloyd have with the "spirit of the five-year plan" that people are so enthusiastic about him? On the whole, the author feels that Harold Lloyd has rejected various ideological attempts; there is not much ideology to be found in his films, but they are full of laughter, so once he stepped into the film industry and eventually penetrated the Soviet screen, he established a solid foundation. His works will probably exist for a long time in Soviet Russia due to their novelty and strangeness. As the saying goes, "the exception proves the rule." Here, we can see a glimpse of the Soviet people's hunger for light entertainment. (The End)
